<div id="review_1204779511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204779511" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27179252-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436920360p2/27179252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204779511?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/27179252-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204779511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13648302454935211717">You can find this review along with many others on <a href='http://www.seamlessreader.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog!</a><br/><br/><div>
  <a href='http://www.seamlessreader.blogspot.com' title='Seamless Reader' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425464482i/13892305.jpg' alt='Seamless Reader' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><br/>When I read the synopsis for this book, I immediately felt keen anticipation for it. It sounded like the kind of book that I would love. I was able to get my hands on it a few weeks ago and now I finally got the chance to read it. And I'm so happy I did.<br/><br/>As opposed to my other reviews, I won't be writing a small summary of the plot simply because I feel like it might spoil the story for you. And I don't want to do that! I do w</span>
  <span id="freeText13648302454935211717" style="display:none">You can find this review along with many others on <a href="http://www.seamlessreader.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog!</a><br><br><div>
  <a href="http://www.seamlessreader.blogspot.com" title="Seamless Reader" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425464482i/13892305.jpg" alt="Seamless Reader" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>When I read the synopsis for this book, I immediately felt keen anticipation for it. It sounded like the kind of book that I would love. I was able to get my hands on it a few weeks ago and now I finally got the chance to read it. And I'm so happy I did.<br><br>As opposed to my other reviews, I won't be writing a small summary of the plot simply because I feel like it might spoil the story for you. And I don't want to do that! I do want to mention all the things I loved about this book. So keep on reading!<br><br>As you might be able to tell from the title, a big part of "Playlist For the Dead" is centered around music. As a music obsessed person, this really made the book even more special to me. I found it to be extremely unique the way that there was a song listed at the beginning of each chapter. It really added substance to the story. I recommend listening to the songs listed while reading the book. You'll thank me later. Also, kudos to the author on her taste in music!<br><br>The writing in this book was impeccable. I really liked how the story flowed perfectly. There wasn't a single dull moment. Everything about the story was gripping and I couldn't put this book down. Which is probably why I finished this in two days. The story is so engrossing, you'll get completely sucked in. It is also very easy to read so there's that! Plus the main character's voice was great and very enjoyable to read. He was awesome as character overall! All of the character's were great, actually. They had depth and really interesting traits that made them all different in their own way. They really influenced my emotions throughout the story which to me is an obvious sign of the books greatness. As well as the author's undeniable talent.<br><br>I am not related nor do I know of anyone close to me that has committed suicide. Hence i don't have concrete knowledge on the subject. However, I do think that the author portrayed the sensitive subject extremely well. It all felt truthful and honest. Including the romantic aspects. Although, the book is centered more around those who are affected by another person's decision to take his/her own life. You see, It focuses more on how to deal with the loss and how to stop blaming yourself. How to get some sort of closure, eventually.<br><br>A real pleasant surprise were the LGBTQ+ aspects in this book! I wasn't aware of this previous to reading the book, but I was ecstatic once I started reading. I feel like this is really growing in the YA community and, personally, I'm all for it. Diversity is definitely needed in YA.<br><br>Everything in this book was well-written and articulated. It was a pleasant but haunting read that will appeal to a lot of people. A lot of it stays with you and arises a lot of thoughts. It's a memorable read; one that'll be circulating in your head long after you finish reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13648302454935211717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1146028247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1146028247" />
    <a title="Melissa Chung" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17703155-melissa-chung"><img alt="Melissa Chung" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427492410p2/17703155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1146028247?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Chung" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Chung" href="/user/show/17703155-melissa-chung">Melissa Chung</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1146028247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5579980558107753767">How to rate this book..... I don't know. I didn't hate it. I didn't love it. So it gets the middle rating. The it was all right rating.<br/><br/>Sam Goldsmith is a sophomore in high school. He has one friend Hayden and Hayden just committed suicide. <br/><br/>I was hoping I would get a better understanding of suicide through the eyes of Hayden's playlist and Sam's discovery of the night Hayden died, but the book didn't fulfill anything I really wanted to know.<br/><br/>Hayden has a learning disorder. Parents that are over ba</span>
  <span id="freeText5579980558107753767" style="display:none">How to rate this book..... I don't know. I didn't hate it. I didn't love it. So it gets the middle rating. The it was all right rating.<br /><br />Sam Goldsmith is a sophomore in high school. He has one friend Hayden and Hayden just committed suicide. <br /><br />I was hoping I would get a better understanding of suicide through the eyes of Hayden's playlist and Sam's discovery of the night Hayden died, but the book didn't fulfill anything I really wanted to know.<br /><br />Hayden has a learning disorder. Parents that are over baring and a bully of a brother. Hayden is slightly over weight. Plays video games, doesn't know how to speak to girls and only has one friend. Sam.<br /><br />Just the thought of Hayden makes me sad. There are kids out there that really kill themselves because of bullies. Because they don't feel worthy enough to live. The whole thought of suicide makes me so angry. What about the people you leave behind? Don't you care how everyone else will feel? It's so selfish to leave this earth because you don't think you are good enough.<br /><br />I guess it isn't just kids that kill themselves. A lot of adults do it too. Being alive is so great! There is music and books and movies and the smell of wet grass and cinnamon baked goods and chocolate. Fuck what others think of you. I'm starting to rant. I don't know anyone who has committed suicide. I have never been in this kind of situation, so I have no room to talk.<br /><br />Back to the review. I gave this book 3 stars because even though it wasn't the best book it made me feel something. It made me angry and sad. <br /><br />I liked Sam's character for the most part. He was showing true grief. Where you go from denial and sadness to anger and blaming yourself. Everyone feels that way. The 'What If's' are in full force when someone close to you passes. I also liked the fact that Sam didn't believe in violence. Even after all that he had seen. He was angry sure, but not once did he want to seriously hurt or kill anyone.<br /><br />It made Sam a real goodie goodie knowing that he had never broken any school rules or kissed a girl or really drank. Then again, he didn't have very many opportunities being a loner.<br /><br />I don't know. I'm on the fence with this book. It was easy to read. Kept me engaged. Had some really good songs that I already love and a few new ones I have added to my own playlist. I just wanted more. Anything. More feeling from everyone else. You learn their stories, you see the outside layer of pain they are going through, but not the struggle. Not like what Sam deals with.<br /><br />I will probably read another of Michelle's books. Like I said the writing wasn't bad I just wanted more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5579980558107753767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1123200403?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin Dunn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin Dunn" href="/user/show/5880366-erin-dunn">Erin Dunn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1123200403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11388822777521033518">It seems to me there has been an influx of YA books on the subject of suicide. Recently I have read Thirteen Reasons Why, I Was Here, and now Playlist for the Dead. As far as Playlist for the Dead is concerned it wasn't as good as the others. Just being honest. It was very mediocre. Are you wondering why then did I rated it 4 Stars? The playlist. Every chapter is a song and in that chapter the song or band is mentioned in some way. What I did was make a playlist and listen to it as I read the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText11388822777521033518" style="display:none">It seems to me there has been an influx of YA books on the subject of suicide. Recently I have read Thirteen Reasons Why, I Was Here, and now Playlist for the Dead. As far as Playlist for the Dead is concerned it wasn't as good as the others. Just being honest. It was very mediocre. Are you wondering why then did I rated it 4 Stars? The playlist. Every chapter is a song and in that chapter the song or band is mentioned in some way. What I did was make a playlist and listen to it as I read the book. When I would start a new chapter I put that song on. I love the music that was picked. I have heard most of the songs/bands already, but not all. IT'S A VERY GOOD PLAYLIST! I feel like with the playlist as a companion to the novel you get a fuller reading/emotional experience. Plus, it adds something fun and different to a meh book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11388822777521033518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1138593306" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138593306" />
    <a title="Jen Ryland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6497049-jen-ryland"><img alt="Jen Ryland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499993823p2/6497049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138593306?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Ryland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Ryland" href="/user/show/6497049-jen-ryland">Jen Ryland</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6497049-jen-ryland?shelf=debut-challenge-2015">debut-challenge-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138593306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer746717880162575839">There were definitely things I enjoyed about this book -- I always love a reading a boy POV and this one was charming though I thought Sam's voice sounded more middle grade than high schooler. <br/><br/>At times I felt there was an awful lot going on - the aftermath of the suicide, the playlist, the mystery attacks, the story of Astrid, the romance, the magical realism... but it definitely had its good moments.<br/><br/>Recommended for those who enjoy a male POV, and issue books with magical realism.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3455874384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3455874384" />
    <a title="Anahita Solot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90492052-anahita-solot"><img alt="Anahita Solot" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585156359p2/90492052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3455874384?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anahita Solot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anahita Solot" href="/user/show/90492052-anahita-solot">Anahita Solot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3455874384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16888645464528732423">I wasn't sure whether to give two stars or three. But I cried for Hayden, so in honors of him, here goes three stars.<br/>This book was ordinary. The author seemed to has never been a teenager. Or has never met a nerd in real life. The story was interesting, and it'd got lots of potentials, but sadly, it was all wasted. The whole process was so slow at some points I wished for Sam to be a little smarter and a little less dense.<br/>Overall, it was a good read but not the most realistic.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1143622057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1143622057" />
    <a title="Jennifer  Ricketts (Donnie Darko Girl)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6097206-jennifer-ricketts-donnie-darko-girl"><img alt="Jennifer  Ricketts (Donnie Darko Girl)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439764474p2/6097206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1143622057?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer  Ricketts (Donnie Darko Girl)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer  Ricketts (Donnie Darko Girl)" href="/user/show/6097206-jennifer-ricketts-donnie-darko-girl">Jennifer  Ricketts (Donnie Darko Girl)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6097206-jennifer-ricketts-donnie-darko-girl?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6097206-jennifer-ricketts-donnie-darko-girl?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6097206-jennifer-ricketts-donnie-darko-girl?shelf=blog-tours">blog-tours</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1143622057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3050723798246891326">I received an ARC of this book from Around the World ARC Tours for my honest review at <a href='http://donniedarkogirl.blogspot.com/2014/12/playlist-for-dead-by-michelle-falkoff.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Donnie Darko Girl</a>. <br/><br/>Having read 13 Reasons Why, I initially thought about that book when I read the synopsis for Playlist for the Dead. I did worry it would be too similar, but it stands on its own two feet with Sam's voice in narrating, the mystery surrounding Hayden's death, and the things Sam learns about himself as well as Hayden. Playlist for the Dead is not only about suicide but also friendship, growing </span>
  <span id="freeText3050723798246891326" style="display:none">I received an ARC of this book from Around the World ARC Tours for my honest review at <a href="http://donniedarkogirl.blogspot.com/2014/12/playlist-for-dead-by-michelle-falkoff.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Donnie Darko Girl</a>. <br /><br />Having read 13 Reasons Why, I initially thought about that book when I read the synopsis for Playlist for the Dead. I did worry it would be too similar, but it stands on its own two feet with Sam's voice in narrating, the mystery surrounding Hayden's death, and the things Sam learns about himself as well as Hayden. Playlist for the Dead is not only about suicide but also friendship, growing up, bullying, and finding your own path amid the pressures from parents, school, and even your friends. <br /><br />The story surrounding Hayden's suicide is messy and complicated, and that's how suicide is. There's never just one reason why a person feels that's their only option; instead there's a myriad of them, and sometimes one event can push that person off the ledge much like the saying about the straw that broke the camel's back. <br /><br />I felt the weight of Sam's guilt settle over me as I read. That was realistically done and as Sam unravels the mystery, he finds more and more people who are also secretly blaming themselves and wrestling with their own guilt, wishing they could have done something to change the outcome. This is one of those times where you wish badly for a rewind button.<br /><br />I believe Hayden felt hopeless about all the bad things happening in his life and didn't have any fight left in him to keep trying for the good. Topped off with the events the night of the party, that was his last straw. Obviously he must have been thinking about suicide as a way out for a while - people don't just wake up one day and kill themselves. It's a slow progression downhill with a lot of time spent struggling, and thinking about all of this just made me feel so much empathy for Hayden. <br /><br />I decided to make the playlist on Spotify and listen to it all the way through then listened to each song for each chapter while I read. I wanted to get into Hayden's mindset when he had made the list. Most of the songs are ones I love already, and I swear I was dissecting lyrics like crazy! I loved the references to Star Wars and especially Donnie Darko along with other geekery sprinkled throughout the story. Geek speak links directly to this girl's heart! <br /><br />No, the answers weren't found in the playlist but it's what led Sam to new experiences and new people. I think it was also a way for Hayden to reach out to Sam after he knew he'd be gone, a way to say good-bye and show him there was more going on with him than Sam realized. I think Hayden wanted Sam to understand how important it is to listen to people, which Sam learns along the way. We all want to be heard. We want to be understood. We don't want to be lonely.<br /><br />I ended up being torn on how many stars to rate Playlist for the Dead. What it came down to for me was I felt something was missing from the story, something I can't quite put my finger on, but it's what made the difference between my feeling that this is a four star read rather than a five star. I do know one part of the mystery could have been wrapped up better. I thought there was so much potential there that wasn't used. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3050723798246891326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QsQpXZi6q0xP5yLsLTRQBJHZT4y9nHjfJPvOf+ST1HweFo3WCr4f6b4N/YP14xb64qubRaMrKbfi3DbbYcMdWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XzL11IqQ3/wnHFppuedZlGCc8KOJEFNcX8r17CSk04cD4FFfGJRrWdb2hQZhMB9qE+4kapenAjSZ7Q1IofQaow==')})
  }

Where we fall. Why we fall.\n\nI understand her sadness and loneliness and silence, her shattered heart.\n\nIt doesn\'t have to be this way, does it?\n\nIt wasn\'t always this way, was it?\n\nStay alive, Liz Emerson, stay alive.\n\nOn the day Liz Emerson tries to die, they had reviewed Newton\'s laws of motion in physics class. Then, after school, she put them into practice by running her Mercedes off the road. Why did Liz Emerson decide that the world would be better off without her? Why did she give up? The nonlinear novel pieces together the short and devastating life of Meridian High\'s most popular junior girl. Mass, acceleration, momentum, force—Liz didn\'t understand it in physics, and even as her Mercedes hurtles toward the tree, she doesn\'t understand it now. How do we impact one another? How do our actions reverberate? What does it mean to be a friend? To love someone? To be a daughter? Or a mother? Is life truly more than cause and effect? After a couple of failed attempts to kill his brother Martin, his parents gave him a guitar for Christmas.\n\nFrom schoolyard battles between the Bowie Boys and the Prog Rockers to Mrs Kemp’s firm insistence on net curtains, and from acting for the Children’s Film Foundation to manning a fruit and veg stall on Saturdays, Gary brilliantly evokes an upbringing full of love, creativity and optimism.\n\nAs the Thatcher years begin, Gary’s account of the outrageous London club scene centred around the Blitz and Billy’s is just sizzling. Out of this glamorous mayhem of kilt-wearing mascara’d peacocks would emerge Spandau Ballet – the band that would define the era, and hold high the victorious standard of the New Romantics.\n\nGary’s thrilling journey with Spandau Ballet would see them record worldwide hits such as ‘True’, ‘Gold’ and ‘Through the Barricades’, play the biggest stadiums in the world and take to the stage in togas when their luggage gets lost in flight. Stallions, supermodels and dwarves would be hired for video shoots, and through it all, Gary records the wonderful friendships, and the slowly-building tensions, that would eventually see five old friends facing each other in court.\n\n‘I Know This Much’ tells the story of Spandau Ballet, but it’s far more than a book about being in a band. Whether it’s meeting Ronnie Kray before filming ‘The Krays’, sketching out the fashions and subcultures of the day, or hanging out with Princess Diana, this book offers a story on every page.         first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>

      </div>

    </div>
